# AMPU — Game Context

> **Batch-13 consolidation.** Written from the codebase + `CLAUDE.md`, then
> updated against **sixteen** formally-ingested forum threads (13 playtest +
> 3 discussion), most recently **batch 13 (`oopscpu`) — a 350-post Ted-run all-CPU
> 1788 CPU-decision-making stress-test** (the second all-CPU run, the canonical
> source for the CPU AI cluster #70–#78 + the post-election Command-loss rule #143
> + the VP-inheritance precedent #61): a 343-post Gilded-Age
> multiplayer playtest (`gilded`), a 732-post 1788 federalism solo-with-AI
> playtest (`federalism`), a 90-post 1772 solo "aesthetic experiment"
> (`1772-solo`), a **2276-post modern (2004→2020) multiplayer 1948 campaign**
> (`modern`), a **9051-post 1856-native multiplayer campaign**
> (`house-divided`, the 1856→1904 alt-history "A House Divided" Part 2), a
> **7540-post all-CPU 1841→1924 playtest** (`drums`, "Drums of War"), a
> **1172-post Era-of-Populism fresh-modern-boot multiplayer** (`pop`,
> "Era of Populism Playtest"), a **9943-post 1800→1868 multiplayer campaign**
> (`rep1800`, "Era of Republicanism 1800–1868" — the **predecessor of `gilded`**,
> same GM `ebrk85`, identical roster), a **3614-post FIRST-MULTIPLAYER 1772
> founding campaign** (`new1772`, "AMPU New 1772 playtest" — 10 humans 1772→1796,
> the only thread that stands up the entire federal apparatus piece-by-piece from
> a 1772 start; **abandoned at GM burnout**), a **157-post solo all-CPU
> 1772→1874 fast-traversal** (`tea1772`, "Stamping out America's love for tea" —
> stalls mid-Gilded, NO future era), and a **12,228-post / 156-chunk modern
> (1948→~2005) multiplayer campaign** (`nuke`, "The Nuclear Age 1948–2004" — the
> **single largest corpus in the KB**; the Cold-War/modern-half new-era gap-fill
> and the direct PREDECESSOR of `modern`, software-truncated at ~2005 mid-page-cap,
> not abandoned), and a **947-post 1820-START multiplayer campaign** (`dem1820`,
> "1820 — The Era of Democracy" — a NEW 1820 scenario start, Monroe's 2nd term /
> late Era-of-Good-Feelings → Jacksonian; **GA-burnout-killed at ~1822-23 in-game**
> after ~1.5 turns, never reaching the 1824 presidential cycle; the **3rd
> independent confirmation of the #92 era-band model from a new start year**) —
> see Sources. "What this game is / Eras /
> Core entities / Glossary" describe the **shipped build** (cited `file:line`).
> The gap log is grouped by area; each row is tagged `ingested` (forum-cited) or
> `codebase`, and notes when a delta is **corroborated across multiple eras** (the
> strongest signal that it is real and load-bearing). A separate **Confirmed
> shipped bugs** subsection lists defects (fixes, not features). The `modern`
> thread is the most mechanically *mature* source; the `house-divided` thread is
> the most mechanically *unique* (1856-native, Civil War / Reconstruction); the
> **`drums` thread is the most mechanically *interior*** — an **all-CPU** run that
> exposes CPU heuristics, thresholds, tie-breaks, and design-holes that prior
> multiplayer threads couldn't capture; **`pop` is the most mechanically
> *initialized*** — the **first fresh-boot of a modern-era scenario** (the
> **scenario-boot model**, gap-log #86); and **`rep1800` is the most
> mechanically *foundational*** — it **fills the entire 1800–1856 early-republic
> gap** (Jeffersonian → Era-of-Good-Feelings → Jacksonian → Manifest-Destiny, an
> era band with NO prior coverage) AND establishes the **★ headline architecture
> finding: eras are content-bands gated by game-state + territory ownership, NOT
> calendar year** (gap-log #92), contradicting the shipped `year % 4` era model.
> **★ Batch 8 makes #92 the single most-corroborated architectural finding in the
> KB: MULTI-SAVE CONFIRMED.** Two fully-independent saves — `tea1772` (1772 start)
> and `rep1800` (1800 start, 28 in-game years apart) — emit the **identical
> era-band labels** (Federalists → Republicanism → Democracy → Manifest-Destiny →
> Nationalism) **at the same in-game dates**, proving the bands are deterministic
> game-state content-gates, not flavor or per-thread GM invention (`tea1772` §2 /
> POST 21, 62, 91, 130, 153; `rep1800` POST 92, 6201). Batch 8 also delivers the
> **first multiplayer 1772** (`new1772`) — confirming the entire founding-era
> apparatus (inaugural draft, Continental/Constitutional Convention, Revolutionary
> War, era-event graph, offices-stood-up-by-law) from a MULTI-FACTION angle, not
> just the batch-2 solo thread. **★ Negative result:** no thread in the corpus
> reaches a "future" era — `tea1772` stalls at 1874 (mid-Gilded) despite its title
> — so "Era of the Future" remains undocumented everywhere (open question).
> The core loop is now **corroborated across 5+ eras / 11 threads**.
>
> **★ Batch 9 (`nuke`) covers the Cold-War / modern HALF (1948→~2005)** — the
> single largest corpus, and the direct predecessor of the batch-3 `modern`
> (2004→2020) thread (read them as one 1948→2020 campaign; the seam is the 2004
> election). Five headlines: (1) **the #92 era-band model now holds across a THIRD
> start year (1948)** — confirmed across **1772 / 1800 / 1948** — and is **refined
> into TWO LEVELS**: point-banked **Historical Eras** (here "Nuclear Age" 1948–2000
> → "Era of Terror" 2000–~2012) vs **decade/census boundaries WITHIN an era** (1972/
> 1980/1990 = bulk EV reallocation + wholesale state-bias re-lean + content rotation).
> **The earlier-extractor "Era of Neocons" band was a MISLABEL — it is a FACTION
> REBRAND + a decade content-rotation, NOT a point-banked band** (logged so it is
> not re-introduced; #92). (2) **The "Cold War" is NOT a system** — it is the
> generic naval→land war engine RELABELED + event-flavor; **no nuclear/MAD/NATO/
> space-race subsystem, no army/navy/air branches, wars never resolve, and the USSR
> NEVER FALLS** (the dissolution chain stalls at a ~5% gate; still a named ally in
> 2005). (3) **The realignment is mechanically-but-GRADUALLY enforced** (4 cooperating
> levers, "1964→early-1990s"), NOT a single scripted flip — and BLUE/RED meaning
> **flips DURING the game** (Dixiecrats start INSIDE Blue). (4) **The ideology scale
> is a CIRCLE** (LW-Pop↔RW-Pop adjacent at 25%) — independently CORROBORATED from a
> SECOND thread (POST 9842; was #99 from `rep1800`). (5) This is the **fullest modern-
> systems capture in the KB** (the primary→brokered-convention→general machine, the
> diplomacy subsystem, first impeachment/resignation/unelected-succession, legislated-
> variable SCOTUS, mutable cabinet, Era-of-Terror content). **★ And the strongest
> corpus statement of design intent: the digital APP is built for 1-human-vs-9-CPU**
> (multiplayer "goes off the rails"), even though `nuke` itself is ~7–10-human MP —
> validating the roadmap's solo-first sequencing (#114). The thread breaks at 2005;
> the **seam to the successor `modern` (2004→2020) is the next likely batch.**
>
> **★ Batch 10 (`dem1820`) is a NEW 1820 scenario start** (Monroe's 2nd term / late
> Era-of-Good-Feelings → Jacksonian "Era of Democracy"), 10-human MP, **GA'd by
> @MrPotatoTed**. It is **short** — opens 1820, runs ~1.5 turns to **~1822-23**, and
> is **GA-burnout-killed in real-time Aug 2025** (Ted quits over player friction; a
> Sept revival reseats the roster and decamps to a new thread) — so it **never reaches
> the 1824 presidential cycle / Jackson / Nullification** (framing, not played).
> Four headlines: (1) **★ #92 is now THIRD-START-CONFIRMED from 1820** — the game's
> own per-faction draft-ideology table prints "**Era of Democracy (1820-1840)**"
> preceding "**Manifest Destiny (1840-1856)**" (the same content-bands the 1772/1800
> saves emit); the era-band model holds across **1772 / 1800 / 1820 / 1948** starts.
> (2) **Polarity = the 1788/1800 alignment** (BLUE = dominant Democratic-Republicans
> / agrarian-states'-rights; RED = dying Federalists / nascent "National Republicans")
> — NOT the 1856 flip; the opening's "brand new National Republican Party" is ~5-10
> yrs anachronistic (RED in 1820 is really the Federalists — historian flag). (3) **A
> rich slice of EARLY-1820s mechanics exercised from a fresh boot:** a live Discord
> draft of 10 marquee picks; the **inaugural career-track seed from the last 3 draft
> classes** (#86/DH-25); **player-controlled SCOTUS** (delay/dismiss is a player
> action, votes are by-ideology — refines #52); a GA-published **meter→enthusiasm→
> election processing rule** (#18/#51); the **House focus-Rep abstraction + seat-locked

> CREATING a game** — GA setup is improvised (a contested undocumented "strip Command
> from ≤40 boot pols w/o a job" house rule; inconsistent career-track-eligibility),

## What this game is

AMPU is a turn-based American political strategy game that runs in the browser
(React + TypeScript + Vite; state persists in IndexedDB). The player runs a
**faction** inside one of two parties (BLUE / RED) and steers it across a
historical timeline: draft politicians, develop them, win elections, staff the
government, pass legislation, fight wars, and resolve era-defining decision
events. There is no single win screen baked in for both scenarios; play is a
campaign across a sequence of phases per turn, with terminal endings on certain
era events (`GameState.gameEnded`, `EraEvent.triggersGameEnd`, types.ts:1476,
1635).

As shipped, AMPU is **single-player**: the human owns exactly one faction
(`Faction.isPlayer`, types.ts:1303; `playerFactionId`, types.ts:1566) and the
engine drives every other faction as CPU. The turn loop is a fixed **phase
sequence** of ~36 phases grouped into 10 categories (`PHASE_SEQUENCE`,
phases.ts:3-47), advanced two years at a time (`nextPhaseInfo` adds 2 per turn
rollover, phases.ts:161). Most systems are **pure functions over a single
`FullGameSnapshot`** (types.ts:1811) in `src/engine/`; the UI is a registry of
~35 pages (registry.ts) with no router.

The engine is deterministic by design (seeded RNG, `src/rng.ts`) and the phase
taxonomy is numbered ("2.1.1 Politician Draft", "2.9.4 Presidential Election",
…) — the same taxonomy the forum game uses, so this build is recognizably an
implementation of that game.

The player's goal is open-ended faction-building: accumulate Political Value
(PV) across your politicians, control offices (Presidency, Congress, governors,
cabinet, courts), shape national meters and interest-group standing, and survive
/ steer the era's crises. **PV drives elections** (`src/pv.ts`; CLAUDE.md).

## Eras & scenarios

The codebase has **four era values** — `independence`, `federalism`,
`nationalism`, `modern` (`Era`, types.ts:1337) — but only **two shipped
scenarios**, and only **three eras are reachable in play**. The forum runs a
**continuous multi-era campaign** (a 1772 or 1800 start runs straight through
independence → federalism → nationalism → gilded → …), with **points reset at
each era boundary** (federalism digest post 518). Eras are not just flavor: each
is a balance dimension *and* carries its own faction roster, nickname table,
draft-ideology profile, era-event spine, bill catalog, card pool, and SCOTUS
case set.

| Scenario | Start | Era(s) reachable | Defining issues | Status |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **1772 — Founding** | 1772, era `independence` (scenario1772.ts:97) | `independence` → `federalism` on Constitution ratification (constitutionalConvention.ts:198) | Independence vs. loyalty, the Revolutionary War, confederation vs. federal union, writing the Constitution | **Built** |
| **1788 — Early Republic** | 1788, era `federalism` | `federalism` (1788–1800) → `nationalism` at ~1800 | **Hamilton vs. Jefferson**: assume Rev-War debt, Bank of the US, US Mint, tariff (set to 10%), bimetallic currency, Militia Act; Compromise of 1790; Whiskey/Fries rebellions; **party-formation as era events** (~1792); French-Revolution wars (War of 1795, Barbary); per-state shift to popular-vote electors; state-by-state slavery abolition vs. Cotton Gin; Louisiana Purchase | **Designed, not built** — now richly documented (federalism digest is the spec) |
| **1800 → Nationalism (the `rep1800` arc, 1800→1868)** | continuous campaign, mid-government boot (`BLUE = Dem-Republicans`, `RED = Federalists→National Republicans` — **party frame inverted** vs later eras) | Forum-internal sub-bands of `nationalism`: **Republicanism (1800–20) → Democracy (1820–40) → Manifest Destiny (1840–56) → Nationalism (1856–68)**; eras advance on **game-state, not year** (#92) | **Republicanism:** British impressment vs France, 12th-Amendment unlock, the 2nd Bank + tariff. **Democracy (Jacksonian):** universal white-male suffrage, the **Bank War**, internal improvements, tariff, slavery. **Manifest Destiny:** Pacific expansion, Texas/Mexican-Cession, slavery-cannot-expand, SC secession threat, Catholic-immigration nativism. **Nationalism:** alt-Civil-War (Pres defects to CSA, UK intervention, guerrilla phase) → Reconstruction | **Designed, not built** — the `rep1800` digest is the spec; **fills the previously-uncovered 1800–1856 gap**. Predecessor of the `gilded` (1868) arc; the 1800 campaign is now documented end-to-end |
| **1856 — Antebellum** | 1856, era `nationalism` (scenario1856.ts:177) | **Shipped:** `nationalism` only (spine ends at the Trent Affair, 1861). **Designed (`hd`):** the same start runs **continuously 1856→1904+** through Nationalism → Gilded (1868) → Progressivism (1892) | Slavery, popular sovereignty / free soil, sectional crisis, **secession & Civil War → Reconstruction** — then forward into the tariff/currency/civil-service/imperialism Gilded issues and the Progressive issue-space | **Partially built** — the antebellum *start* ships, but the **Civil-War combat engine, Reconstruction subsystem, secession-trait gating, sectional-balance crisis, and Canada/era-continuation** are designed-not-built (`hd` digest is the spec; gap rows #56–#69) |
| **1800 → Gilded Age (1868–1892)** | continuous campaign | Reaches a `gilded`-style era (likely the `modern` enum, or its own value) | **Tariff** (national integer set by legislation); **currency** (Gold-Standard vs Bimetallism/Free Silver); **civil-service reform / anti-corruption** ("Honest Gov't" crisis); **imperialism** (island naval bases); Native-relations bills; Chinese / Jewish immigration bans; women's suffrage (state-by-state); Jim Crow / Poll Tax / Prohibition policy switches | **Designed, not built** — confirmed by the gilded digest |
| **1948 → Modern (the `nuke`+`modern` arc — one campaign family 1948→2020)** | a **1948 mid-20th-c. boot** (the `nuke` thread runs 1948→~2005; `modern` continues 2004→2020) | The full **`modern`** era, split into the two-level era model: point-banked Historical Eras **"Nuclear Age" (1948–2000) → "Era of Terror" (2000–~2012) → Populism (2012–2024)**, with per-decade census boundaries (1972/1980/1990) inside each | **Most mechanically mature era.** Modern issue menu (tariff power to the President, income-tax brackets, healthcare, immigration, climate, Wall Street, gun control, surveillance/drone/detention); the **named meter bank + enthusiasm/Party-Pref engine**; **full primary→brokered-convention→general** subsystem; **named-Justice SCOTUS docket** (legislated-variable size, court-packing, compelled votes); modern legislative depth (Crisis Bills, packaging, Executive-Branch-Interference, investigations, mutable cabinet); 53-state alt roster (DC/Cuba/PR) under a Wyoming-Rule apportionment; **the realignment** (Dixiecrats inside Blue → modern polarity by ~1980); diplomacy (8 named nations); the **generic war engine relabeled** as the Cold War | **Designed, not built** — `nuke` backfills the **1948→2004 origin** (the fullest modern capture); `modern` is the 2004→2020 continuation |
| **"The next era" (post-1892, pre-modern)** | implied | unknown | Feminists, socialists, communists, prohibitionists, eugenicists, labor activists — narrated as forthcoming in the Gilded-Age era brief | **Designed, scope unclear** |

The forward arc is therefore **nationalism → gilded → progressive → … →
modern**: the `nationalism` Civil-War scenario is built, but the gilded/
progressive/modern eras at the end of the timeline are only `modern`-enum tuning
rows with no scenario. **federalism** sits *between* the two built scenarios and
is well-documented (`fed`); the **modern** end-state is now the best-documented
unbuilt era (`modern` digest — a 2276-post campaign).

**Alt-history note.** The forum campaigns are **alternate timelines**, not
re-enactments. The `modern` campaign began at **1948** and 60 in-game years of
player decisions produced a divergent present: a **53-state** union (DC, **Cuba**,
**Puerto Rico** are full states), ahistorical presidents (Cuomo, Kirk, a 3-term
Cochran), and ahistorical SCOTUS rulings (Janus/Atkins/Dobbs all decided
differently, flagged "ahistorical"). The game runs on **its own clock**, with
**fictional era names** ("Era of Terror" …–2012, "Era of Populism" 2012–2024) and
events firing ~10 years behind real tech. Real history supplies *texture and the
menu of plausible issues*; outcomes, officeholders, and the enacted-law record are
the campaign's own. (Per historical-context.md §10, the **modern era is the one
window where BLUE=Democrat=left / RED=Republican=right with no polarity caveat**,
and the shipped flat interest-group pool — Big Tech, Big Oil & Gas, Globalists,
LW/RW Media, anachronistic in 1856/1868 — **fits here**.) `modern` 426, 1080,
2067; historical-context §10.

- **1772** is a long "expansion-style" inaugural draft: the entire politician
  pool is drafted snake-order (scenario1772.ts:86, 107-117); historical founders
  enter via the CSV-driven inaugural draft, not the seed roster. It starts with
  **no government** — no president, no cabinet, no governors, no courts — which
  unlock through era events (Declaration → governors; Constitution → presidency,
  courts, cabinet). Era-event spine (eraEvents1772.ts): Intolerable Acts,
  Lexington & Concord, Continental Army, Alliance with France, Declaration of
  Independence, Articles of Confederation, Treaty of Paris, Annapolis →
  Constitutional Convention, plus westward events (Vermont, Fort Stanwix).
- **1856** starts **mid-government**: Buchanan is president, the Constitution is
  ratified, governors and courts exist (scenario1856.ts:179-193). It begins past
  the draft phase (`phaseId: '2.1.2'`, scenario1856.ts:153). Era-event spine
  (eraEvents1856.ts): Bleeding Kansas, Dred Scott, Panic of 1857, Southern
  Secession Threat, Secession Winter (1860–61), Trent Affair.
- **Era is also a balance dimension**, not just flavor: many rule tables are keyed
  by `Era` — mortality multipliers (`MORTALITY_RULES.eraConfig`, types.ts:507),
  faction-leadership churn (`LEADERSHIP_RULES.eraConfig`, types.ts:460), anytime-
  event rates (`ANYTIME_EVENTS_RULES.eraConfig`, types.ts:1076), and several
  trait election/governance effects are era-scaled. `modern` rows exist
  throughout but no shipped scenario reaches that era.

## Core entities & systems (index)

One line each; see `game-mechanics.md` for the actual rules/math.

- **Politician** (types.ts:1251) — the unit. Has `skills` (6 keys, 0–5),
  `command`, `traits[]`, `expertise[]`, `ideology`, faction/party, age, office,
  career track, PV cache, loyalty. **Drafted, never hand-placed** in 1772.
- **Skills** (types.ts:24) — `admin, legislative, judicial, military, governing,
  backroom`, integers 0–5.
- **Command** — a separate combat/leadership stat (not in `Skills`), gates
  kingmaking and military command.
- **Traits** (types.ts:62) — ~60 positive/negative tags (Charismatic, Integrity,
  Corrupt, Iron Fist, …) added over time (PR4b/PR6 batches), with symmetric
  conflict pairs (`TRAIT_CONFLICTS`, types.ts:658) and election/governance
  effects (`TRAIT_ELECTION_EFFECTS`, `TRAIT_GOVERNANCE_EFFECTS`).
- **Expertise** (types.ts:182) — a third axis, 19 policy domains (Economics,
  Foreign Affairs, Military, Labor, …), granted by office/career/lobby.
- **Ideology** (types.ts:5) — 7-point scale `LW Populist … RW Populist`; drifts
  and can be deliberately shifted.
- **Career tracks** (types.ts:43) — 7 tracks; politicians accrue skills/traits/
  expertise over up to 20 years on a track (phase 2.1.2).
- **Faction** (types.ts:1293) — what the player runs. Belongs to a party, has a
  `personality` (LW/Center/RW) and three card decks: `ideologyCards`,
  `lobbyCards`, `interestCards`. Factions drift alignment over time (phase 2.1.8).
- **Party** (types.ts:1306) — two: BLUE and RED. Meaning is **era-specific**
  (see glossary).
- **State** (types.ts:1318) — 13 colonies (states1772.ts) or 31 states
  (states1856.ts); has region, electoral votes, `bias`, `industries`, senators/
  reps/governor; 1772 colonies carry `ccDelegateSlots`/`colonySize`. The `region`
  enum already includes `Caribbean`/`Latin America`/`Pacific`/`Atlantic` — partial
  readiness for the modern 53-state alt roster (DC/Cuba/PR as states; gap-log #55).
- **Offices** (`OfficeType`, types.ts:1111) — President, VP, 7 cabinet seats
  (era-gated by year, `cabinetSeatsForYear`, types.ts:1196), General-in-Chief /
  Admiral, Chief/Associate Justice, Senator, Representative, Governor, Speaker,
  Pro Tem, Committee Chair, Faction/Party Leader, CC President, Ambassador.
- **Elections** (`calcStateVote`; `ElectionContext`, types.ts:697) — 6 contexts:
  presGeneral, presPrimary, house, senatePre17 (both eras use pre-17th-Amendment
  legislature-elected senate), governor, internalParty. PV-driven.
- **Legislation** (types.ts:1506) — factions propose bills routed to one of four
  committees (Domestic/Foreign/Economic/Justice), committee review, then House +
  Senate floor votes (phases 2.6.1–2.6.3).
- **National meters** (`NationalMeters`, types.ts:1399) — revenue, economic,
  military, domestic, honest, quality, planet; tick in the Lingering phase (2.5.1)
  and via events/legislation. The forum's modern bank adds **Party Preference**,
  **per-power relation meters** (8 powers), and **per-ideology enthusiasm** to this
  set, with crisis/cascade rules (gap-log #50).
- **Interest groups / enthusiasm / party preference** — `InterestGroupScores`,
  `Enthusiasm` (ideology×party −5..+5), `partyPreference`: the electoral mood
  substrate. The forum drives these via a formalized **4-part enthusiasm-reshuffle
  + faction-Score** engine (gap-log #51).
- **Era events** (`EraEvent`, types.ts:1466) — interactive scripted decisions
  (phase 2.4.3) with a `decider` (president/congress/cabinet/cc-president/auto)
  and effect-bearing responses; some unlock systems or end the game. 1772 also
  has a data-driven **precondition graph** (`Predicate`, types.ts:1487;
  `ERA_GRAPH_RULES`).
- **Anytime events** (phase 2.4.2) — non-scripted historical/scandal events
  (anytimeEvents.ts, anytimeNationalEvents.ts), era-rate-scaled.
- **Era systems (1772 only, in the build):** Continental Congress
  (`ContinentalCongress`, types.ts:1347; built via phase 2.9.6), Revolutionary
  War (`RevolutionaryWar`, types.ts:1371; battles in 2.7.2), Constitutional
  Convention (`ConstitutionalConvention`, types.ts:1801; sets
  `ConstitutionalArticles`). **Design intent:** war is a *generic* cross-era
  system (War of 1795, Barbary, 1812) — see gap-log #45 — and Constitutional
  change continues post-founding via durable **Amendments** (gap-log #39).
- **Player meta-systems (per-turn passes, phases 2.1.3–2.1.8):** Flip-Flopper
  cleanup, Relocations, Ideology Shifts, Faction Conversions (poaching/signing),
  Kingmakers & Protégés, Faction Personalities/Alignment drift. Each has its own
  rule const block and event feed in types.ts.
- **Cabinet & loyalty (PR5/PR6)** — cabinet appointments scored per seat
  (`CABINET_SEAT_SCORING`); 1856 cabinet members carry `loyalty` that decays in
  the Secession Winter event and can trigger defection.
- **Draft dataset** — bundled "standard draft classes" are **generated** by Node
  scripts (`scripts/`), ~18.5k politicians runtime-loaded from
  `public/standard-draft-classes.json`; users can import custom draftees
  (`ImportedDraftee`, types.ts:1780). Do not hand-edit generated files.

## Glossary

- **PV (Political Value)** — a politician's weighted worth, office-weighted;
  the currency that drives elections (`computePV`/`refreshPv`, src/pv.ts).
- **BLUE / RED** — the two parties; **meaning is era-specific.** 1772: BLUE =
  Patriots / Anti-Federalists, RED = Federalists (factions1772.ts:27-28). 1856:
  BLUE = Democratic Party, RED = Republican Party (factions1856.ts:19-22). Do not
  assume a fixed left/right reading across eras.
- **Faction personality** — `LW | Center | RW`, the faction's coarse lean;
  distinct from a politician's 7-point `ideology`.
- **Era** — engine bucket (`independence/federalism/nationalism/modern`), a
  superset of scenario; used for balance scaling, not just narrative.
- **Half-term / turn** — the loop advances 2 years per full pass of the phase
  sequence; `HalfTermSummary` (types.ts:1762) records per-turn deltas.
- **senatePre17** — election context: both shipped scenarios predate the 17th
  Amendment, so senators are chosen by state legislatures, never popular vote
  (types.ts:696-703).
- **electorsByLegislature** *(early-republic, `rep1800`)* — a proposed per-state
  flag (sibling of `senatePre17`): pre-12th-Amendment, many states choose
  presidential electors by **state legislature**, so the EV winner is decided by
  **who holds Gov/Sen/Rep** (majority party; Gov breaks ties), **not** by PV+dice.
  Phases out per-state by amendment/event; the "Nationwide Popular-Vote Surge" era
  event flips all-but-SC. Distinct from #44's `electionMethod`. `rep1800` §2-A.
- **Content-band era** *(architecture, `rep1800`)* — the design's actual notion of
  an "era": a fixed **band of available bills/events/draftees + a state-bias
  table**, entered/exited by **game-state + territory-ownership** triggers, NOT by
  calendar year. The clock runs ~30 yrs behind content (LA Purchase fires 1834).
  Contradicts the shipped `year % 4`/`year % 2` predicates. See gap-log #92.
- **Internal era names** *(era-sensitive, `rep1800`)* — the forum's eras are
  **finer-grained** than the 4-value `Era` enum: Republicanism (1800–20) →
  Democracy (1820–40) → Manifest Destiny (1840–56) → **Nationalism** (1856–68).
  The first three are **sub-bands of the shipped `nationalism` enum**;
  "Nationalism" internally = antebellum/Civil-War = the shipped `nationalism` value.
- **Cohens-v-Virginia precedent** *(early-republic, `rep1800`)* — an ahistorical
  scripted SCOTUS ruling that **federal law does NOT supersede existing state
  law**, making slavery a **state issue**: a slave state's slavery can be ended
  **only by a constitutional Amendment** (or a per-state Gov action). The engine
  substrate for the whole sectional design; there is **no mechanism to reverse an
  ahistorical ruling**. `rep1800` §2-B.
- **Command** — combat/leadership stat outside the 0–5 skill set; gates military
  command and kingmaker eligibility (`KINGMAKER_RULES.commandGateByScenario`).
- **Kingmaker / Protégé** — a high-Command mentor anoints a young protégé who
  graduates to higher office after ~20 years (`KINGMAKER_RULES`, types.ts:295).
- **Lingering phase (2.5.1)** — per-turn drift of national meters based on
  cabinet/conditions.
- **Sub-floor stats** — failed candidates / era figures in the dataset get
  deliberately weak electoral stats so they rarely win (CLAUDE.md dataset rules).
- **Lobby / Ideology / Interest cards** — the three faction card decks that
  define a faction's coalition and shift over time (types.ts:1298-1300).
- **Southern Unionist (trait) / Secessionists (pool)** *(1856-arc, `hd`)* — on
  secession, pols of seceded/border states go inactive into a "Secessionists"
  pool **unless** they hold the `Southern Unionist` trait; they return on the
  state's readmission. The draft dataset carries the trait on Southern pols.
- **Reconstruction +2-Red bias** *(1856-arc, `hd`)* — a time-boxed (8-yr,
  sunsetting) per-state partisan bias toward the incumbent party, granted by the
  Ironclad-Oath readmission plan; distinct from the permanent `State.bias`.
- **Acting President** *(1856-arc, `hd`)* — when the elected line fails (e.g. a
  foreign-born Speaker is ineligible), the Senate Pro Tempore acts; a **0-Command
  acting president is inert** (no exec actions, can't compel SCOTUS, can't be
  elected). The succession order is itself legislatable.
- **Primary Group (1–5)** *(Primary Era, `hd`)* — states opt into presidential
  primaries (via a Gov action) and are bucketed into 5 sequentially-voting groups;
  once any state opts in, the Primary Era begins (primaries precede conventions).
- **War Score** *(`hd`)* — per-theater Civil-War tally (+1 win / +3 Difficult land
  / −1 loss); **+10 auto-wins the theater**, else a carry-roll continues the war
  next half-term.

## Built vs. Designed — gap log

The heart of this doc; the roadmap is built from this. Rows are grouped by area.
Each is tagged `ingested` (forum-cited via a digest under
`docs/game/playtest-digests/`) or `codebase` (derived from the AMPU source
tree). Digest shorthands: **`gilded`** = the f4c7c2c4 1868 Gilded-Age digest;
**`fed`** = the f55d3e21 1788 federalism digest; **`1772s`** = the 85f8e6b4
1772 solo "aesthetic" digest; **`modern`** = the 3a9ac985 1948-campaign **2004→2020 successor** digest;

(cited `hd I-n` for its Part-I unique-system sections, else `hd POST n`);

> **DEFECTS vs. GAPS.** This table is *missing features* (designed-but-unbuilt).
> Outright **bugs in shipped behavior** live in the separate "Confirmed shipped
> bugs" subsection below — the roadmap should treat those as fixes, not
> features.

### Platform / cross-cutting

| # | Area | In the build today | In the documented design | Delta / requirement | Source |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | **Multiplayer** | Single-player: one human faction (`isPlayer`), all others CPU (scenario1772.ts:64, scenario1856.ts:121) | **Multiplayer** — 8–10 human drafters across 2 parties (5 Blue + 5 Red), with handles; CPU factions only fill empty seats; **factions are transferable between humans mid-campaign** and CPU is a true per-faction fallback (`modern`: a new player took a CPU faction and won the presidency days later; `pop`: `Vee01` took R5 mid-thread, won the 2016 GOP nomination). (Both solo threads, `fed` + `1772s`, confirm the *same game* is also played solo-with-AI — so solo and multiplayer are two modes of one engine) | Multi-faction human control / turn arbitration; per-player handle + identity; async/seated turns; GM-style narration layer; CPU only as fallback; faction-handover support. (**7+ era confirmed** — very high confidence). **★ BUT the strongest design-intent statement (`nuke`) says the digital APP is 1-human-vs-9-CPU** (multiplayer "goes off the rails") even though the forum game is team MP — so the build is a **solo adaptation of a multiplayer game**; see #114. **`nuke` 1948 boot:** ~7–10 humans, **5 RED + 5 BLUE**, CPUs fill VACANT factions only (suffix `CPU`), humans rotate in/out. **`dem1820` 1820 boot:** 10 humans, **5 BLUE + 5 RED** (the cap holds an 8th era); **2 mid-thread handovers** (RingTheDink→Saucialiste; Euri CPU'd twice for absence) + CPU backfill — confirms faction transfer + per-faction CPU fallback | ingested (gilded 1, 12, 26, 113, 298; fed 1, 12; 1772s 1, 11; modern 1, 7, 424, 444; **hd 1, 38, 153, 456, 875**; **pop 1, 17, 24, 303, 312, 320; 1856-native + fresh-modern**; **nuke / POST 1, 16-17, 33, 483, 6966-6970; see #114**; **dem1820 POST 1, 412-414, 591, 601**; **terror2000 — CPU-heavy 2000-start: GA offered all-CPU / one-human-faction-each / 4-player setups (POST 1); started 8 humans + 2 CPU (RedCPU/BlueCPU), then BOTH CPU factions were handed to humans mid-thread (RedCPU→@ConservativeElector2, BlueCPU→@Pius XIII, POST 658-664) — CPU-as-per-faction-fallback + faction-handover, exactly the `oopscpu`/`nuke` pattern**; **modernday — 8 humans (4 Blue / 4 Red, NOT 5/5; the 5th-slot factions ran CPU all game: `ButtigiegCPU`/`HestiaCPU`/`BrunnellCPU`); GM CPU-substitutes inactive players "using CPU rules" (POST 55, 160, 852); mid-thread + era-boundary handovers (`pman` takes the Haley faction; the whole GM role itself handed Rodja→ebrk85; `Vicx`/`MrPotatoTed`/`ShortKing`/`pman` rotate in at the 2024 boundary, POST 1899-1910); CPU factions auto-accept the era-boundary faction-trade (POST 1949)**) |
| 2 | **Eras covered** | Two scenarios: 1772 + 1856. `modern` era unreachable | A **continuous campaign** spanning independence → federalism → nationalism → Gilded Age → … → modern; points reset at each era boundary; the **card-count economy rescales** at each boundary; **end-of-era point awards** are paid out. **`rep1800` runs the early half of this arc end-to-end** (1800 boot → Republicanism → Democracy → Manifest Destiny → Nationalism → 1868) and captures the **full era-boundary machinery** at the "End of Historical Era" phase: (1) **faction-trade window** (CPU factions auto-accept); (2) **point-banking** (most-points +5; most-points-OTHER-party +3; 2nd-if-same-party +3; ALL top-party factions +3; −1 if an allied faction finishes last/next-last); (3) **non-banked points reset to 0**; (4) new-era issue brief; (5) **draft order = just-completed-era points only** (not cumulative); (6) wholesale **new per-era state-bias table** | Continuous multi-era timeline (or chained scenarios w/ state hand-off); era enum likely needs `gilded` + `progressive` (AND the early sub-bands of #92); per-era card-count table + era-end award rules; **a ~12-step era-boundary boot pipeline** (#68) with the explicit faction-trade / point-banking-formula / reset / draft-order-by-last-era / per-era-bias steps from `rep1800`. (**7-era confirmed**; `fed` 518 + `modern` 1080/1172 + `hd` live transitions at 1868 & 1892 + **`rep1800` captures the boundary formula verbatim** + **`modernday` fires it LIVE at the 2024 Populism→Near-Future boundary** — points bank per era) | ingested (gilded 1; fed 11, 518; modern 1, 769, 1080, 1106, 1172; hd I-12, 2151, 2441, 6679-6816, 6681; **rep1800 §B 6187, 6201, 6203, 6421; §A 3167**; **★ modernday — LIVE boundary banking (ch26 POST 1871, see #68); the GM also printed the canonical 14-band era→start-year→first-president map (POST 2964): Independence 1774 / Federalism 1788-Washington / Republicanism 1800-Jefferson / Democracy 1820-Monroe / Manifest-Destiny 1840-Harrison / Nationalism 1856-Buchanan / Gilded 1868-Grant / Progressivism 1892-Cleveland / Normalcy 1916-Wilson / Ideologies 1928-Hoover / Nuclear-Age 1948-Truman / Neocons 1972-Nixon / Terror 2000-Bush / Populism 2012-Obama — corroborates #92 and confirms each band is a poll-able start point**) |
| 4 | **Era-specific ideology drafting profile + off-profile/adjacency rules** | Static seed factions per scenario; no per-era drafting profile | Each faction's drafting ideology mix updates per era (gilded: Brocklin Lib/Mod → Prog/Lib; federalism is a heavily Mod/Cons era; modern: the class is hand-tuned to include "some moderates"). **`rep1800` adds the early-era profile + the mechanics:** the Republicanism/Democracy era pool is **Mod/Cons/Trad/Lib-heavy — "Progressives don't really exist in this era"** (Blue carries the LW end); each faction has **assigned draft ideologies** (Nikk = LW-Pop/Prog; Red = Cons+Trad); **off-profile picks succeed at only 30%**, and once the profile pool is exhausted **adjacent ideologies become 100%** | Per-(faction, era) drafting profile + the 30%-off-profile / 100%-adjacent-on-exhaustion rule, or a drift rule at era boundary. (**5-era confirmed**) | ingested (gilded 1; fed 136, 330; modern 460, 1088; **rep1800 §A 1659; §B 5140, 6203**; **nixon1972 — a 1972-start STILL enforces draft-ideology restrictions: off-ideology draft attempts roll >50 to succeed (many fails; Yellen 95/70 success, POST 109-120), and once a faction exhausts its profile pool it gets adjacent ("border") ideologies "without penalty" (POST 109, 111). ★ CONTRAST trump2024 (Ted, designer): a 2024 board has NO draft-ideology restrictions at all (see NEW #171) — so the restriction is itself era-keyed: ON in early/realigning eras, OFF in the modern present**) |
| 92 | **★ Eras-as-content-bands gated by game-state (NOT calendar year) — MULTI-SAVE CONFIRMED across 1772/1800/1820/1948; TWO-LEVEL model** | `Era` is a 4-value enum (`independence/federalism/nationalism/modern`, types.ts:1337); era predicates are pure calendar — `isDraftYear`/`isPresidentialYear` = `year % 4`, `isElectionYear` = `year % 2` (phases.ts:49–58); `shouldRunPhase` keys off the year | **THE headline architectural delta — now the most-corroborated finding in the KB.** An "era" is a **fixed band of available bills/events/draftees + a state-bias table**, advanced by half-term at a **game-state boundary**, NOT by calendar year — and **content is gated by TERRITORY OWNERSHIP**: bills/events/draftees for un-owned land are *invalid* (Indian Removal gated behind owning LA; Louisiana-born pols undraftable until LA owned). `rep1800`'s clock runs ~30 yrs behind its content (LA Purchase fires calendar 1834). **★ MULTI-SAVE CONFIRMED (batch 8):** the **1772-start `tea1772`** save and the **1800-start `rep1800`** save — two fully-independent campaigns begun **28 in-game years apart** — emit the **identical named era-bands at the same in-game dates** (Era of Federalists ~1800 → Age of Republicanism ~1820 → Era of Democracy ~1840 → Era of Manifest Destiny ~1856 → Era of Nationalism ~1868), each scored at its boundary. Transitions are game-state-gated, not annual (the CW band opens on an era event + DomStab/secession, not a date; Reconstruction ends piecemeal by legislation). The bands are **start-scenario-independent** (a 1772 start still closes Nationalism ~1868 on post-Reconstruction game-state). The forum's internal early eras (**Republicanism / Democracy / Manifest-Destiny**) are **sub-bands of the shipped `nationalism` enum**. **★ THIRD START CONFIRMED (batch 9, `nuke`):** the same engine runs in the MODERN half from a **1948 start**. **★ FOURTH START CONFIRMED (batch 10, `dem1820`):** a **1820 start** prints the identical per-faction draft-ideology bands — "**Era of Democracy (1820-1840)**" preceding "**Manifest Destiny (1840-1856)**" (the early sub-bands of `nationalism`) — so the model now holds across **1772 / 1800 / 1820 / 1948** starts. **★ TWO-LEVEL refinement (`nuke` settles a partial-digest conflict):** there are **two distinct mechanics**, an earlier extractor conflated them: **(a) point-banked Historical Eras** = the big content-bands (the original #92 mechanic): here **"Nuclear Age" = ONE era 1948–2000 → "Era of Terror" 2000–~2012**, entered at a **2000 point-banking boundary** with explicit "now that we are in the Era of Terror…" rule deltas; the *transition trigger* is the calendar year hitting 2000, but the *content/scoring/rules* are era-gated. **(b) decade/census boundaries WITHIN an era** (1972/1980/1990) = a SEPARATE schedule-fired mechanic doing THREE things at once: bulk **EV reallocation** state-by-state, **wholesale state-bias re-lean** (Blue5..Tossup..Red5), and **content rotation** (draft pool / lobby cards / era-activated industries). **★ CORRECTION — logged so it is not re-introduced: "Era of Neocons" / "Corporate Republicans" is a FACTION REBRAND (~1980–82) + a decade content-rotation label, NOT a point-banked band** (the shared sheet's tabs loosely name it, conflating decade-rotation with "era"; the digest is authoritative). So the design needs **finer-grained era bands than the 4-value enum**, a **two-level model (point-banked Historical Eras + per-decade census/content boundaries within each)**, AND a **game-state/territory-ownership era-advance condition** in place of `year % 4` | **Top-priority architecture row.** Decide: era bands gated by game-state + territory ownership (the design) vs the shipped `year % 4` predicates; sub-band the early eras under `nationalism` (Republicanism/Democracy/Manifest-Destiny) or add enum values; add a **territory-ownership content filter** on bills/events/draftees (pairs with #33/#43/#60 territory gating + BUG-1 era-event scheduling). | 108 | **★ The realignment is enforced mechanically but GRADUALLY (4 cooperating levers, NOT a single scripted flip); BLUE/RED meaning flips DURING the game** | Seed factions are static per scenario; | 114 | **★ Design intent: the APP is SOLO (1-human-vs-9-CPU); the forum game is team MP — the build is a solo adaptation** — NEW | Build IS already single-player (one `isPlayer` faction, 9 CPU) — this row VALIDATES the shipped shape against design intent (most other rows are MP-vs-solo deltas) | **The strongest corpus statement of the digital app's intended mode.** The designer states the computer game is built for **1 human vs 9 CPU** because human multiplayer "goes off the rails"; the points system is for CPUs + enthusiasm, not humans (low points = better draft order, so humans could tank it). | 8 | **Committee block-and-replace + chair-blocks-one + repeating-bill auto-block** | Bills proposed → committee → floor (phases 2.6.1–2.6.3). Chair eligibility requires prior committee service (`modern`: **Leadership OR Legis ≥ 2**). Bills marked with a star/`##` are block-eligible. **`pop` confirms a clean chair-blocks-ONE rule** (POST 487-490): chair may BLOCK exactly **one proposal** from the slate **before** the vote, then the committee votes on the rest. Also: **repeating-bill committee auto-block** — if the same legislation is proposed twice in the same cycle, the Chairman auto-blocks the duplicate (`pop` POST 712-714) | Add committee-chair "block-and-replace" action with same-committee replacement check + chair-eligibility gate + **chair-blocks-exactly-one-pre-vote** + duplicate-bill auto-block. (**6+ era confirmed**; pervasive — `hd` sharpens the rule: a chair may replace only a bill whose **proposer has LESS Legislative AND lacks Efficient**; `pop` confirms in fresh-modern boot) | ingested (gilded 160-163; fed 160, 209, 305, 380, 563, 723; modern 46, 285, 1312, 1870; **hd 195-203, 469, 5123**; **pop 487-490, 712-714**) |
| 9 | **Bill packaging / bundling** | Each bill votes separately | Chair can package multiple committee bills into one floor vote that passes/fails as one; **packages can't be split-voted** (`modern` 1341). Federalism nuance: a chair **won't bundle** a net-negative bill *unless* it's a statehood bill; CPU bundles ~75%. Used as a weapon (`modern`: pair a poison-pill with a desired bill so both die). **`pop` reconfirms** in a fresh-modern boot: after committee votes, chair **packages passing bills together OR leaves them separate** (POST 502-507) — load-bearing weaponization, **4 unrelated GOP bills jammed into Bill #3** to amortize sign/veto cost (POST 507, 542) | Add packaging + vote aggregation; bundling-eligibility rule; no-split-vote constraint. | 106 | **★ The "Cold War" is NOT a system — it is the generic war engine RELABELED + event-flavor (no nuclear/MAD/NATO/space subsystem; USSR NEVER falls)** — NEW | No Cold-War / containment / nuclear subsystem; `revolutionaryWar.ts` is the only war code (1772-scoped) | **The single biggest modern-half structural finding.** Despite the "Nuclear Age" title there is **NO purpose-built Cold-War subsystem** — only the **same naval→land d100 battle engine (#45) relabeled** with era-appropriate war names (US–Spain/Franco, the "Korean War" run as the Vietnam-quagmire stand-in to its ~17th–19th year, GOP-opened Cuba/Cambodia/Somalia/Rwanda, Gulf War, Early War on Terror) + scripted **event-flavor**. **NO nuclear / arms-race / MAD / space-race subsystem** (nukes = a Soviet-Nuclear-Test event + one "2× points for nuke/mil bills next session" multiplier; NASA = a bill + a prerequisite flag; NATO/détente/SALT/Berlin/Watergate are one-off A/B point-swing events, not systems — Watergate even fires **no impeachment trigger**). The war engine has **no army/navy/air branch separation** (army generals command navies; "naval" pols die in infantry attacks) and **wars never resolve on their own** (end-roll odds so low the Korean War ran ~two decades; **white peace rarely possible** — most wars have no Treaty B/C authored). **★ The end of the Cold War is NOT modeled — the USSR NEVER FALLS:** the clock crosses 1982→2005 with no fall-of-USSR / German reunification / peace dividend; the USSR is a **live named ally + diplomatic actor in 2004–05** (a sitting Ambassador to the Soviet Union; the Soviets launch Mir as a current event; "Russo-Georgian War" treats Russia as "the USSR, a nuclear power"). The dissolution event-chain exists but is gated (Solidarity → JPII → Glasnost → SDI → **Gorbachev ~5% gate — never cleared** → 1989 20% → Dissolution 10%) and **never fired** ("we keep missing the 5% chance"). Cold-War-end triggers are also buggy (only Dissolution/Soviet-Alliance explicitly end Cold-War status; an LW-Pop early alliance would prevent the Cold War triggering at all) | This is **negative scope** for the roadmap: do NOT build a bespoke Cold-War/nuclear/MAD/NATO/space subsystem — model the Cold War as (a) the generic war engine (#45) + (b) scripted events/event-flavor + (c) the diplomacy meters (#107). BUT the **war engine needs branches + a real resolution model + white-peace rules** (DH-47), and the **USSR-collapse / Cold-War-end trigger chain must be re-tuned so it can actually fire** (DH-45). Pairs with #45/#107 + DH-45/DH-46/DH-47 | ingested (**nuke §4 / POST 494-500, 1101-1102, 1234, 2599-2609, 6266-6272, 6354-6358, 6674-6676, 7097-7099, 9745, 9796, 11055, 11058-11060, 11398, 11466, 11706, 11750-11752**; **terror2000 CORROBORATES the relabeled-engine modern-native (War on Terror + War in Afghanistan run the SAME d100 naval→land engine, no MAD/nuke subsystem, Air-Force/Marine generals are naming-only POST 50-56) AND refines "wars never resolve on their own": here the War on Terror DID RESOLVE — in DEFEAT (POST 639, see #152) — and Afghanistan ran to Phase II; so wars CAN end, incl. in loss; Iraq War never fired (timeline diverged)**; **nixon1972 — a 1972-start pins the Watergate gate: "75% chance to fire with a president who has CONTROVERSIAL" / "Can't fire, controversial is required" (POST 16, 18) — confirms Watergate = a Controversial-gated ~75% EVENT (no impeachment trigger), exactly as this row states; never fired live (thread stalled in turn 1)**) |
| 107 | **★ Diplomacy subsystem — 8 per-nation relation meters + ambassador action menu + détente/summit exec actions + a Diplomacy phase (the real, working Cold-War part)** — NEW | A Diplomacy phase exists (#26) but no per-nation relation ladder, ambassador roster, or summit/détente actions | **The working modern foreign-affairs system** (vs the non-system #106). **8 per-nation relation meters** (UK, France, Spain, Germany, Russia/"Soviet Union", China, Japan, Israel) on a **9-point ladder** (Hostile < Enemy < Neutral < Friendly < Allies). Each nation has a **standing Ambassador** (cabinet-level appointment; eligibility = Admin 2+ & Business/Foreign-Affairs/Trade; can't send to a Hostile-or-worse / at-war nation; **Naive-Strategist trait = −1 to every ambassador roll**). In the **Diplomacy phase (2.7.1)** the Sec of State *suggests* one action per ambassador; the President approves/overrides; each ambassador sent once/phase. **Ambassador actions:** Increase Relations (±1), Increase Trade Relations (≥neutral → +rev/budget), Extend Credit / **Take a Loan** (≥neutral; +rev/budget; tracked on a Loans/National-Debt credit-debt scale, **gated by the Rev-Budget level** to stop a debt-manipulation exploit), Provoke (≤neutral; −1 relation + 1–2% war chance, needs Congress until the Pres has full tariff power). **Détente/summit EXEC actions:** "First President to Visit the USSR", "Détente Policy w/ USSR" (+1 Russia), US–USSR Summit (25%/25% improve/worsen, +to 35% with Foreign-Affairs/Sec-State 4–5). **Cold War status hard-caps Russia/China relations ≤ Neutral while active.** **EraEvo "wars" (Six-Day, Yom Kippur, Coup in Haiti) are pure relation-meter ±1 flavor**, distinct from engine wars (#45/#106) | Add a **diplomacy module**: 8 per-nation relation meters (era-dependent roster, #25b) + a standing-ambassador appointment slot per nation + the ambassador action menu (Increase/Trade/Credit/Loan/Provoke, rolled by Admin, with the Naive-Strategist + send-once + can't-send-to-hostile gates) + a credit/national-debt scale gated by Rev-Budget + détente/summit exec actions + Cold-War relation hard-cap. **BUT the meters need downward pressure** (DH-46 — currently "allied with everyone"). | 39 | **Constitutional Amendments as durable, separately-ratified state — MUTATE CORE RULES** | `constitutionalConvention.ts` covers the *initial* Constitution; later amendments not surveyed | Amendments pass Congress then go **to the states for ratification**. A **grandfather clause** can exempt the sitting officeholder. **★ `rep1800` makes the rule-mutation concrete — amendments rewrite the constitutional shape MID-GAME**: the **"Sexenio" experiment** ratified 3 amendments in 1834 that turned the Presidency into a Mexico-style **single 6-year term** (16th = Universal White Male Suffrage; 17th = One-Term Limit; 18th = Six-Year Term), with a 25th-style succession rule (a VP elevated past the half-way point can't run); terms later reverted by amendment. **No grandfather clause modeled** (the real 22nd exempts the incumbent; GM: "my rules" — design hole). | 100 | **SCOTUS can OVERTURN a ratified Amendment (review/repeal loop) + threshold-itself-amendable** — NEW | Amendments treated as durable (#39); no judicial-review-of-amendment path; no mutable amendment threshold | **★ A ratified constitutional Amendment is NOT final — SCOTUS can strike it.** Via a **Governor-requested judicial review**, the Court can **overturn a ratified Amendment** (`tea1772`: the timeline's 13th "White-Male Suffrage" Amendment was overturned **4–3**, reverting it to a mere governor-action that Congress may re-pass; a Taylor-McDowell law was similarly overturned). ### Modern macro-state, enthusiasm engine & SCOTUS (NEW — mostly modern-era)

The prior threads saw meters/enthusiasm/SCOTUS in pieces; the `modern` thread
supplies the concrete, mature specifications below — the spine of the modern
election engine.

| # | Area | In the build today | In the documented design | Delta / requirement | Source |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 50 | **The named meter bank (concrete set) + crisis/cascade rules** | `NationalMeters` exists (types.ts:1399): revenue, economic, military, domestic, honest, quality, planet | The concrete modern bank, each on a **banded-text ladder** nudged ±1 by phases/cabinet/"Lingering"/"Revision to Mean"/"Volatility"/legislation: **Revenue-Budget, Economic Stability, Military Preparedness, Domestic Stability, Honest Gov't, Quality of Life, Planet's Health, Party Preference** + **per-ideology enthusiasm** + the **8 per-power relation meters**. Dropping a meter into a bad tier **begins a named Crisis** with knock-ons; recovery ends it; meters **cascade** (one level caps/forces another); top-of-meter has hard rules (**Honest Gov't maxed deactivates all Political Machines + Gerrymandering**). **`pop` confirms the bank in a fresh-modern-boot:** rev/budget, Economic Stability, Honest Gov, Quality of Life, Domestic Stability, Military Prep, Planet Health, Party Pref, per-ideology enthusiasm, per-power relations all tick in Lingering | Verify the shipped meter set matches; add banded-text ladders + crisis entry/exit by tier + cascade rules + top-of-ladder effects. (**5+ era confirmed** — modern is the canonical spec; **`hd` corroborates across a 2nd era and extends it — see #67 for the full ~16-meter bank** + the 9-part Lingering resolution + policy-gated caps; **`pop` confirms in a fresh boot**) | ingested (modern 12, 114, 618, 721, 1238, 1537, 1962, 2230; **hd I-12**; **pop 463-464, 525, 539, 542, 544, 567, 681, 1124**) |
| 51 | **Faction-enthusiasm / Party-Preference election engine** | `Enthusiasm` (ideology×party −5..+5) + `partyPreference` exist; the driving algorithm is not in code | Every ideology holds an **enthusiasm position on a Blue↔Red track**; **Party Preference** is the master partisan meter. After legislation scoring a fixed **4-part rule** reshuffles enthusiasm by which faction gained most/least for the dominant vs opposition party. A running **faction Score** drives this and pays **end-of-era awards**; a team's **lowest-scoring faction penalizes teammates**. "State of the Meters" then maps the whole bank → per-election bonuses (#18). **`drums` independently confirms the 4-step loop across a 3rd era** (POSTS 50, 86, 295, 442, 2537, 2726, 2879, 3115) — (1) events award/penalize per-faction; (2) **most-points dominant faction shifts +1**; (3) **least-points dominant faction shifts -1**; (4) **most-points opposition +1 / least-points opposition -1**; per-faction enthusiasm shifts: dominant ±1, others ±1 per faction-level comparison. **Era-end scoring rewards** (POST 4477): +5 most points, +3 second, etc. **±3 cap on per-phase ideology swings** (POST 4574) — Tyler patched mid-thread; Mods swung +7 raw → capped at +3. **Cabinet enthusiasm-via-lobbies overwhelms presidential signal** without cap (POSTS 877, 880). **`pop` reconfirms in a fresh-modern boot:** per-ideology enthusiasm ±/Party Pref ticks every phase (debate +1, scandal -1, convention strong-ticket +1, October Surprise +1, Planet Health crisis -2 multi-ideology); confirms the same 14-dim per-ideology engine drives the modern arc | Implement the 4-part enthusiasm-reshuffle algorithm + faction Score economy + era-end awards + lowest-faction penalty + **±3 per-phase ideology-swing cap**; wire to the meter→election map. (**5-era cpu-confirmed; ★ FORK-RESOLVED**) | ingested (modern 96, 134, 722, 768, 945, 1080, 2039; **hd 1394, 1568, 6535, 7799, I-12**; **drums 50, 86, 295, 442, 877, 880, 647, 813, 979, 1880, 2537, 2726, 2879, 3044-3065, 3115, 4477, 4574**; **pop 53, 212, 220, 223, 232, 234, 242, 463, 543, 567, 972**; **arkzag — ★ SETTLES the `dem1820` #18/#51 fork: the final chunk publishes the 4-step rule VERBATIM and it MATCHES `drums` (not Ted's "every state" nor Matt's "primaries only"): per Congress's by-card→by-faction legislation tally — (1) faction with MOST pts for dominant party → cards +1 enth toward dominant; (2) LEAST pts for dominant → −1 away; (3) MOST pts for opposition → +1 toward DOMINANT ("taking care of their needs"), only if it gains pts; (4) LEAST pts from opposition → +2 toward OPPOSITION ("furious at incumbent"), even if it gains pts — shifts STACK; paired w/ a meter-overflow ±cap. ### Antebellum / Civil-War / Reconstruction systems (`hd` + `rep1800`)

The `house-divided` thread is the **first 1856-native procedural record** of the
antebellum → Civil-War → Reconstruction → Progressive-finale machinery. **`rep1800`
now corroborates these rows from a SECOND, DISTINCT campaign with DIVERGENT
outcomes** (a different Civil War: fires ~1846 off DomStab=1 not a secession
convention; the President defects to lead the CSA; UK-intervention theater; a
guerrilla 4th stage; National Republicans not Whigs) — strong independent
confirmation that the engine is one ruleset, plus new variant content. The shipped
`scenario1856.ts` / `eraEvents1856.ts` spine **ends at the Trent Affair (1861)** and
has none of this — the war these campaigns play is host-improvised content.

| 99 | **Ideology scale is a CIRCLE (LWPop↔RWPop adjacency) — THREE-THREAD CONFIRMED + Ted-RULED** | `Ideology` is a linear 7-point type `LW Populist … RW Populist` (types.ts:5); shifts/conversions assume a line | A **mid-era rule change wraps the 7-point ideology scale into a RING**: **LW Populist ↔ RW Populist shifts are allowed at 25% base** (the two ends become adjacent), and **conversions extend to adjacent ideologies** (same-party other-faction pols of same OR adjacent ideology — was same-only earlier). ### CPU AI specifications (NEW — `drums`-derived, **`oopscpu`-corroborated**; resolves DH-8 heuristics)

The `drums` all-CPU playtest is the **first explicit forum record of CPU
heuristics**. The shipped game is single-player; **every faction except the
player is CPU**, so these rows are first-class build requirements. They
**RESOLVE the bulk of DH-8** (CPU AI under-spec); the REMAINING DH-8 gaps live
in DH-19..DH-22 below. **★ Batch 13 (`oopscpu`) is the second all-CPU run and
the first DELIBERATE CPU-ruleset interrogation** (Ted-run, explicitly "to find
where the rules are insufficient" — POST 1, 5). It **corroborates #70/#72/#73/
#74/#75/#76 from a founding-era angle**, adds **NEW CPU sub-gaps OC-1..OC-8**
below, and pins several **Ted rulings** (the post-election Command-loss rule, the
pre-12A CPU nomination trio, the help-allies gov-term sub-rule). **Coverage
caveat: the convention CPU AI (#71) is UNTESTED by `oopscpu`** because the 1788
pre-12A era runs no conventions — leadership IRV (#70) is the only convention
proxy here. **Shipped reality:** the engine has CPU code for the meta-passes
(draft pick / career track / relocation / ideology shift / conversion — see
`phaseRunners.ts` `RELOCATION_ODDS.cpuGate`, `IDEOLOGY_SHIFT_ODDS.cpu`) but
**none of the #70–#78 handler suite** — those remain designed-only.

| # | Area | In the build today | In the documented design | Delta / requirement | Source |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 70 | **CPU leadership / Speaker / PPT IRV bloc-vote + 3-inconclusive-ballot collective endorse** | Leadership phase exists; no CPU bloc-vote model | Authoritative IRV tie-break ladder confirmed across **4+ maps** (Speaker, PPT, Sen Maj/Min Leader/Whip, House Maj/Min Leader/Whip elections): (1) ballot 1, each faction casts as a UNIT for own/closest candidate; (2) **closest ideology**; (3) **highest PV**; (4) **highest Legislative skill**; (5) random same-party as last resort. **After 3 inconclusive ballots, CPUs collectively endorse a winner** (confirmed POSTS 5272, 5841, 6099). Designer patches: **continuous IRV elimination** (no ballot-3 random collapse, POST 3419) + **randomize only on FIRST elimination** (POST 3419). **No reciprocity / vote-trading exists** (POST 4875 — designer comment "the CPUs don't understand reciprocity"). Closest-ideology can flip leadership to the minority party (POST 3419, Magoffin/Cons-Dem 1880). Southern) rolled to SUPPORT the **Abolish-Slavery-by-Compensating-Owners CRISIS bill** on crisis-resolution grounds → **slavery abolished by 1792, no secession, no divisiveness** (Ted: "feels too easy… a 60-80 year fiercely divisive issue irl yet in the game it's ho-hum"). | OC-4 | **★ CPU drafts strong rookies OUTSIDE its ideology (no ideology-distance gate on the draft)** — NEW | The draft auto-pick has a 25% "go for the best pol meeting the rolled goal even off-ideology" branch; no distance cap | `oopscpu` POST 227-228, 234-237: both **left-of-center** factions headhunted **Andrew Jackson (RW Pop)** — "25% chance CPU will try when there's a better pol meeting their rolled goal (highest PV) outside ideology." ### NEW mechanics surfaced by `pop` (fresh-modern-boot deltas)

The `pop` thread is the **first record of how a modern-era scenario BOOTS from
cold** (vs. `modern`'s 60-yr continuation from a 1948 campaign). It surfaces a
small cluster of HIGH-signal mechanics around the **scenario-boot model** + the
**Era-of-Populism mechanical surface** that the modern-era flat card pool
configures rather than introduces. These are net-new rows; the bulk of `pop`
**corroborates** §22 systems already in the gap log (see #1, #8, #9, #10, #12,
#47, #50, #51, #52, #67 strengthened above).

| # | Area | In the build today | In the documented design | Delta / requirement | Source |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 86 | **Scenario-boot model (mid-government, pre-built sheet, era-tuned faction decks)** — NEW | Two shipped scenarios: 1772 (cold draft) + 1856 (mid-government at phase 2.1.2). No formalization of the boot-shape pattern | A **single canonical boot shape** for mid-government scenarios (**1788 designed / 1856 shipped / 1800 in `rep1800` / 2012 fresh-modern in `pop`** — now 4 instances), constructed from a **single pre-built sheet**: (a) **two parties, 5 named factions each** (B1-B5, R1-R5; the per-party-5-faction cap holds **7+ eras**); (b) **archetype politicians + era-tuned ideology + interest + lobby decks per faction at boot** (R1 deck = "Trumpism" RW Pop + Trad + Nationalist + Protectionist + RW Media + Isolationists; B1 deck = "Bernie-populism" LW Pop + Reformist + Welfare + Public Housing — **the era identity is EMERGENT from the seed decks, not a new code path**); (c) **sitting government pre-loaded** (`pop` Obama+Biden+7-Dept cabinet+50-state Congress+9 SCOTUS; ### Early-republic systems (NEW — `rep1800`-only; the 1800–1856 gap-fill)

The `rep1800` thread is the **first procedural record of the 1800–1856 early
republic** (Jeffersonian → Era-of-Good-Feelings → Jacksonian → Manifest-Destiny).
The rows below have no shipped representation and were not surfaced by the prior
seven threads. The headline architecture finding lives in #92 (cross-cutting);
these are the era-content + subsystem deltas. Several **refine** existing rows
(noted) rather than duplicate — dedup is hard here.

| # | Area | In the build today | In the documented design | Delta / requirement | Source |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 93 | **12th-Amendment before/after state machine (conventions + VP-on-ticket are unlocked, not always-on)** | No 12th-Amendment toggle; conventions (phase 2.9.2) + VP exist unconditionally; no `electorsByLegislature` flag | A genuine **era-specific state machine** absent from all post-12A threads. **PRE-12A:** **no conventions at all**; many states pick presidential electors **by legislature** — for those the EV winner = **who holds Gov/Sen/Rep** (majority party; Gov breaks ties), **NOT** PV+dice (a per-state `electorsByLegislature` flag, sibling of `senatePre17`; in 1804 CT/GA/MA/NJ/NY/SC/VT were legislature-decided). **Passing the in-game "President Elections by Party Tickets Amendment" (= the 12A)** is the single toggle that **unlocks conventions + the separate VP-on-the-ticket** rule (and gates "Separate VP Election" + "Send VP to Shore Up Support", confirming #91). The **"Nationwide Popular-Vote Surge" era event** later flips **all states except SC** off legislature-electors — the end-state of the machine. Also the **first fully-recorded FIRST convention** (resolves `gilded` open-Q #10) | Add the 12A as a **toggleable amendment state** that gates conventions + VP-on-ticket; add a per-state `electorsByLegislature` flag flipped off by amendment/the popular-vote-surge event; pre-12A EC = state-control tally not PV+dice. Pairs with #39/#44/#91 + the convention subsystem #13 | ingested (**rep1800 §2-A, §A 222, 264, 276, 502, 638, 691, 708, 2468; §B 6650**; **new1772 reaches the SAME machine organically from a 1772 start — pre-12A ALL candidates run for President and the top 2 become Pres/VP (no conventions); passing the "President Elections by Party Ticket Amendment" turns on conventions + running mates for 1796; pre-12A EVs split between legislature-decided states (vote by Kingmakers/Gov) and a popular-vote subset; §2h+§5 / POST 1981-1987, 2296, 2665, 3460**; **arkzag — the holdouts persist into the 1820s-40s: in the 1828 presidential election DE + SC still choose electors by LEGISLATURE ("Delaware/South Carolina: Legislature selects [candidate]", ch15 POST 1253-1257) while every other state runs the d6 popular vote**) |
| 94 | **Slavery = persistent state flag tied to Plantation + Cohens-v-Virginia amendment-only abolition** | `SLAVE_STATES_1856` const + `State` exists; **no `State.policies` flag** (per #21); no scripted-ruling rule-modifier on legislation | **Slavery ON/OFF is a persistent state-level policy flag tied to the Plantation industry** (extends #21's Jim-Crow/poll-tax pattern *backward* — the gap-era flag is `slavery`/Plantation): a successful abolition bill turns OFF Plantation nationwide + permanently deactivates all slavery legislation; abolition "counts" only when NO state has it active. **★ The ahistorical `Cohens v. Virginia` SCOTUS precedent holds federal law does NOT supersede existing state law** → slavery is a **state issue**, abolishable **only by a constitutional Amendment** (or per-state Gov action); existing slave states keep it, all new states/territories enter free, spread halts. **This is the engine substrate for the whole sectional design** (feeds #59's free/slave-balance crisis) — and there is **no mechanism to reverse an ahistorical ruling** (cross-thread AMPU-2 need) | Add `slavery`/Plantation to #21's `State.policies` set with the nationwide-off-on-abolition behavior; model the **scripted-SCOTUS-precedent-as-persistent-legislation-rule-modifier** (`Cohens` blocks legislative abolition until an Amendment) + a ruling-reversal-via-amendment path. | 95 | **Second Bank of the US: recharter clock + Bank War exec action + unremovable Bank-President office** | No Bank model; cabinet seats are year-keyed (`cabinetSeatsForYear`, types.ts:1196), fixed | The Bank is a **toggleable, cabinet-seat-granting institution with a 20-yr recharter clock** (created as a Crisis Bill; **recreates the President-of-US-Bank office, which is UNREMOVABLE while the Bank exists**; must be rechartered within 20 yrs or it lapses). The 1772 solo thread exists specifically to prototype the **look and feel** of
the eventual computerized AMPU. Its thesis: *a political sim wearing
fantasy-sports / trading-card clothes with an old-school almanac vibe.* None of
this is a deliberate visual language in the shipped UI (functional pages only).

| # | Area | In the build today | In the documented design | Delta / requirement | Source |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| A1 | **Politician portrait / art pipeline** | `Politician` (types.ts) has no image/portrait field; no card view | Hand-authored art for marquee figures + **CK2-style procedural portraits** for the ~18.5k long tail. **Hard stance: no AI-generated imagery or text in the shipped product** (AI used only as a proof-of-concept stand-in). **`modern` reinforces:** the dataset runs out in deep-modern → procedurally-generated pols (#43) need procedural portraits too, so the portrait system must cover *generated* pols, not just the real dataset | Add a portrait field + a procedural-portrait system covering generated pols; commit to no-AI-in-product art direction | ingested (1772s 13, 14, 51, 860; modern 456, 1771) |
| A2 | **Canonical ideology→color palette (cross-cutting)** | `components/Meter.tsx` colors meters; no documented 7-ideology palette reused everywhere | A canonical ideology→color mapping (Prog/Lib/Mod/Cons/Trad/RW-Pop legend) used consistently across roster, congress, maps, score sheets. Color-coding is core to both *reading* and *playing* (it makes Committees tractable) | Define + apply one ideology→color palette app-wide | ingested (1772s 12, 25, 70, 71) |

## Confirmed shipped bugs

**Defects in existing behavior + design holes** (roadmap = fixes, not features).
`BUG-*` are shipped-code defects (surfaced by `fed`, verified against the codebase
where quick); `DH-*` are **GM-confirmed rules gaps / design holes** from the forum
where the rulebook had no answer (these are design defects to spec, not crashes).

| # | Bug | Symptom | Root cause / status | Source |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| BUG-1 | **Era events don't deactivate for non-1772/1856 start years** | A scenario whose **start year is past an era** still has that era's events in the roll table, *and* (per the official ruling) events deactivate **only** if the start year is past the era — so e.g. an **1800-start game wrongly loses the Louisiana Purchase**. Stale events also dilute the roll table | The 1856 path calls `buildEraEventsForYear(year)` with **no era-vs-start-year filter** (phaseRunners.ts:2817). **Latent in the shipped build** (only 1772/1856 ship today) but a hard blocker the moment a federalism/1800 scenario is added. Wants an "era-lock" filter (unbuilt, fed posts 524, 535). Official ruling: `@Ich_bin_Tyler`, post 524 | ingested (fed 521-535; **rep1800 LIVE-CONFIRMS this exact bug: the GM found the Louisiana Purchase was listed under the prior Era of Federalism and so was “not included” for an 1800-start game; he hand-added it in 1816 — verbatim §A POST 2668. Independent same-class confirmation; DH-30 is the companion event-scheduler-min-floor fix**) |
| BUG-2 | **`Chisholm v. Georgia` lacks an "11th Amendment not ratified" gate** | The SCOTUS case should be gated on the 11th Amendment not yet being ratified | **Case not yet in the build** — no SCOTUS case data file contains it (grep: 0 hits in src). So this is a *forward requirement on the SCOTUS-case content*, not a live crash today. Logged to the dev's Basecamp by the forum | ingested (fed 145-150) |
| BUG-3 | **No fallback when there is no viable PM General candidate** | If no eligible politician exists for the PM General / `GeneralInChief` cabinet seat, the procedure is undefined → potential crash (player hand-waved with a "Hand of God" stat bump) | `GeneralInChief` is a real seat (types.ts:1121) gated by `cabinetSeatsForYear` (types.ts:1196), but the no-candidate path isn't covered. **Reported, crash-path unverified** — escalated to the dev (fed post 5) | ingested (fed 5, 119) |
| DH-1 | **A filibustered "MUST-pass" bill has no rules remedy** | The GM can declare a bill "MUST pass" (e.g. a required tariff each session); when the required tariff bill was **filibustered to death**, the rulebook had **no remedy**. The GM **improvised** a "special committee" of the 4 congressional leaders who must agree on a tariff that auto-passes, dropping EconStab + applying election penalties **per day until they agree** (an "AMPU government shutdown") | **GM-confirmed rules gap — VERIFIED in-thread** (GM explicitly flagged it to fix). The shipped engine needs a defined rule for a failed required/MUST-pass bill (deadlock-resolution: forced compromise, shutdown penalty clock, or fallback auto-pass) | ingested (modern 640, 696, 711, 716) |
| DH-2 | **Modern era-event deck appears decoupled from the literal year** | In the ~2018 turn the EraEvos deck pulled **2008-era cards** (Subprime Mortgage Crisis, ABM/INF treaties) — events fired years out of phase with the campaign clock | **Possible bug — REPORTED, not verified.** Could be intended shuffle/backlog or a scheduling defect; reconcile with BUG-1 (era-event scheduling/era-lock) and the era-event scheduling-model open question | ingested (modern 2221) |
| DH-3 | **Career-track pols can run for President** | A career-track pol is barred from Gov/Rep/leadership/Kingmaker but **no rule bars a presidential run** | **GM-acknowledged rules gap, intended-to-fix, unbuilt.** Bar career-track pols from the presidential candidate pool (and from CPU presidential selection) | ingested (hd 8205-8219; relates to #63) |
| DH-4 | **"Extend Credit to all nations" near-auto-win foreign loop** | Diplomacy "Extend Credit" is per-nation | **Balance flag:** extending credit to all 7 powers "works amazingly every time" — a positive trade balance with all nations triggers a stacked bonus (EconStab→Booming + random industry + random foreign relation). Needs a diminishing-returns / cap rule | ingested (hd 7346; relates to #26/#27) |
| DH-5 | **Kingmaker-flip grabs the protégé(s) — "insanely OP"** | Kingmaker/Protégé pairing exists (#design) | **Balance flag:** converting/flipping a Kingmaker also seizes his protégés (and their +1 election standing) — flagged "insanely OP." ## Open questions

_Resolved by batch 2:_ **era cadence**, **foreign-relations roster** (era-dependent),
**faction card-distribution algorithm** (`1772s` B9). _Confirmed/extended by batch
3 (`modern`):_ the **meter set** (concrete bank + crisis/cascade), the
**enthusiasm/Party-Pref engine** (4-part reshuffle), the **full presidential
subsystem**, the **SCOTUS subsystem**, **amendment ratification by governors
(40/53) + 2/3-House**, and the **8-power relations roster (+Israel)**.
_Resolved/clarified by batch 4 (`hd`):_ the **era-boundary point question** —
points **DO bank per era** via a ~12-step boot pipeline (#68); the **per-party
faction cap** = **5 Blue + 5 Red** holds across a 5th era; the **amendment
ratifier/threshold is era-keyed AND in-game-tunable** (3/4 Governors in 1856 →
2/3 default later, #64); the **investigation spec** now has a concrete 5d6 rule
(#65, fills #54). _Resolved/clarified by batch 5 (`drums`):_ **the bulk of DH-8
(CPU AI under-spec) is now resolved** — explicit heuristics for candidate
selection (#72), leadership IRV (#70), convention behavior (#71), cabinet
selection (#73), legislation voting (#74), scripted-event A/B/C cabinet voting
(#75), conversion %-table (#76), faction-leader replacement (#78), and the
faction-rename trigger (#40). DH-8 **REMAINS open** for the architectural gaps
DH-20/DH-21/DH-22 (no vote-trading, no meter-guarding, no event-cascade
smoothing). The **Justice 10-yr drift percentages** (25/10/5 mid/left/right) are
now canonical (#79); **±3 swing cap** is patched (#80); **veto override = 2/3
both chambers** (#82); **midterm uses full meter+enthusiasm** (#83); **contingent
election rules don't exist** (#84 — author before build); **5%/half-term
retire/death** (#85). _Resolved/clarified by batch 6 (`pop`):_ the **scenario-boot
model** is now documented (#86 — pre-built sheet, era-tuned faction decks, no
inherited legacy); a **NEW meter-driven endgame condition** (Planet Health
APOCALYPSE 10-yr clock, #88); the SCOTUS confirmation rule is sharpened to a
**declarative auto-AYE-within-1-step rule** (#52); **bills-create-cabinet-seats**
generalized across eras (#89); **procedural-pol-gen is era-coded by rule 3.0.18**
(#90, pairs with #43 dataset-exhaustion); **era-coded double-points scoring**
(#87). DH-24..DH-28 added (boot-data quality, career-track bootstrap, 3rd-party
trait, trait-conflict in boot data, meter-tag completeness). _Resolved/clarified by batch 7 (`rep1800`):_ the **1800–1856 early-republic gap is FILLED end-to-end** (Republicanism → Democracy → Manifest-Destiny → Nationalism → 1868; predecessor of `gilded`) and the **★ headline architecture finding** is logged — **eras are content-bands gated by game-state + territory ownership, NOT calendar year** (#92, contradicting the shipped `year % 4`/`year % 2` predicates).
